# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've completed the comprehensive analysis of the Envoy ADS (Aggregated Discovery Service) gRPC server implementation. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I've identified all C++ source files in envoyproxy/envoy that implement the ADS gRPC server and created a detailed answer at `/workspace/answer.json`. The implementation consists of **34 key files** organized into several functional areas:

### Core Components:

1. **gRPC Mux Implementation** - Manages multiplexing of multiple resource types (EDS, CDS, LDS, RDS) over a single stream:
   - Modern modular implementation in `xds_mux/` directory
   - Legacy implementations for backwards compatibility

2. **Delta xDS State Machine** - Implements incremental update protocol with per-resource versioning

3. **SotW xDS State Machine** - Implements state-of-the-world protocol with full resource snapshots

4. **gRPC Stream Handler** - Manages bidirectional streaming to the xDS server with rate limiting

5. **Resource Subscription Tracking** - WatchMap manages which resources are being watched by Envoy components

6. **ACK/NACK Processing** - PausableAckQueue ensures proper ordering of acknowledgments with pause/resume support

7. **Failover Support** - GrpcMuxFailover handles switching between primary and backup xDS sources

8. **Service Definitions** - Protocol buffer definitions for StreamAggregatedResources and DeltaAggregatedResources RPC methods

The answer includes file paths, key symbols (classes), the call chain for message processing, and detailed narrative documentation explaining the architecture and data flow.

Envoy always prefers fetching config from the\\n12:  * primary source, but if not available, it will fetch the config from the failover\\n13:  * source until the primary is again available.\\n14:  *\\n15:  * This class owns the state for the GrpcMux primary and failover streams, and\\n16:  * proxies the gRPC-stream functionality to either the primary or the failover config sources.\\n17:  * The failover source is optional and will only be used if given in the c'tor.\\n18:  *\\n19:  * Failover is supported in both\\n20:  * SotW (RequestType = envoy::service::discovery::v3::DiscoveryRequest,\\n21:  *   ResponseType = envoy::service::discovery::v3::DiscoveryResponse), and\\n22:  * Delta-xDS (RequestType = envoy::service::discovery::v3::DeltaDiscoveryRequest,\\n23:  *   ResponseType = envoy::service::discovery::v3::DeltaDiscoveryResponse).\\n24:  * Both the primary and failover streams are either SotW or Delta-xDS.\\n25:  *\\n26:  * The use of this class will be as follows: the GrpcMux object will own an instance of\\n27:  * the GrpcMuxFailover. The GrpcMuxFailover will own 2 GrpcStreams, primary and failover.\\n28:  * Each of the primary and secondary streams will invoke GrpcStreamCallbacks\\n29:  * on their corresponding objects (also owned by the GrpcMuxFailover). These invocations\\n30:  * will be followed by the GrpcMuxFailover calling the GrpcStreamCallbacks on the GrpcMux\\n31:  * object that initialized it.\\n32:  *\\n33:  * To simplify the state-machine, Envoy can be in one of the mutually exclusive states:\\n34:  *   ConnectingToPrimary - attempting to connect to the primary source.\\n35:  *   ConnectedToPrimary - after receiving a response from the primary source.\\n36:  *   ConnectingToFailover - attempting to connect to the failover source.\\n37:  *   ConnectedToFailover - after receiving a response from the failover source.\\n38:  *   None - not attempting to connect or connected to any source (e.g., upon  initialization).\\n39:  *\\n40:  * The GrpcMuxFailover attempts to establish a connection to the primary source. Once a response is\\n41:  * received from the primary source it will be considered available, and the failover will not be\\n42:  * used. Any future reconnection attempts will be to the primary source only.\\n43:  * However, if no response is received from the primary source, and accessing the primary has\\n44:  * failed 2 times in a row, the GrpcMuxFailover will attempt to establish a connection to the\\n45:  * failover source. Envoy will keep alternating between the primary and failover sources attempting\\n46:  * to connect to one of them. If a response from the failover source is received, it will be the\\n47:  * source of configuration until the connection is closed. The GrpcMuxFailover will own 2 GrpcStreams, primary and failover.\n28:  * Each of the primary and secondary streams will invoke GrpcStreamCallbacks\n29:  * on their corresponding objects (also owned by the GrpcMuxFailover). These invocations\n30:  * will be followed by the GrpcMuxFailover calling the GrpcStreamCallbacks on the GrpcMux\n31:  * object that initialized it.\n32:  *\n33:  * To simplify the state-machine, Envoy can be in one of the mutually exclusive states:\n34:  *   ConnectingToPrimary - attempting to connect to the primary source.\n35:  *   ConnectedToPrimary - after receiving a response from the primary source.\n36:  *   ConnectingToFailover - attempting to connect to the failover source.\n37:  *   ConnectedToFailover - after receiving a response from the failover source.\n38:  *   None - not attempting to connect or connected to any source (e.g., upon  initialization).\n39:  *\n40:  * The GrpcMuxFailover attempts to establish a connection to the primary source. Once a response is\n41:  * received from the primary source it will be considered available, and the failover will not be\n42:  * used. Any future reconnection attempts will be to the primary source only.\n43:  * However, if no response is received from the primary source, and accessing the primary has\n44:  * failed 2 times in a row, the GrpcMuxFailover will attempt to establish a connection to the\n45:  * failover source. implementation is located in the source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc directory of the envoyproxy/envoy repository. The implementation consists of several key components:\\n\\n## Core gRPC Mux Implementation (xds_mux namespace)\\n\\nThe newest and most modular implementation is in the xds_mux subdirectory (source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/). This includes:\\n\\n1. **GrpcMuxImpl (grpc_mux_impl.h/cc)** - A templated base class that manages subscriptions to one or more resource types. It implements two concrete variants:\\n   - GrpcMuxDelta: Implements Delta xDS protocol (incremental updates)\\n   - GrpcMuxSotw: Implements State-of-the-World xDS protocol (full resource snapshots)\\n   Both handle multiplexing multiple resource types (EDS, CDS, LDS, RDS) over a single gRPC stream.\\n\\n2. **Delta xDS State Machine (delta_subscription_state.h/cc)** - Tracks the protocol state of delta xDS sessions for individual resource types. Manages:\\n   - Requested resource tracking with per-resource versions\\n   - Wildcard vs specific resource subscriptions\\n   - Resource TTL (time-to-live) for heartbeat support\\n   - Subscription interest changes\\n\\n3. **SotW xDS State Machine (sotw_subscription_state.h/cc)** - Tracks state-of-the-world xDS sessions, managing version information and resource updates.\\n\\n4. **Subscription State Base Class (subscription_state.h)** - Provides the abstract BaseSubscriptionState template that both delta and SotW implementations inherit from. Handles:\\n   - ACK/NACK generation via getNextRequestWithAck()\\n   - Response handling through handleResponse()\\n   - Error detail formatting for rejections\\n\\n## gRPC Stream Handler\\n\\n**GrpcStream (grpc_stream.h)** - Manages the bidirectional gRPC stream to the xDS server. It:\\n- Establishes and maintains the connection\\n- Receives discovery responses via onReceiveMessage()\\n- Sends discovery requests\\n- Handles rate limiting and backoff strategy\\n- Implements Grpc::AsyncStreamCallbacks interface\\n\\n## Resource Subscription Tracking\\n\\n**WatchMap (watch_map.h/cc)** - Tracks subscriptions to xDS resources:\\n- Manages \\\"watches\\\" from different Envoy components (e.g., listeners, clusters) for the same resource\\n- Tracks which resource names are currently of interest\\n- Delivers updates to all interested watches\\n- Manages EDS resources cache for endpoint discovery\\n\\n## ACK/NACK Processing\\n\\n**PausableAckQueue (pausable_ack_queue.h/cc)** - Manages the queue of ACK/NACK messages:\\n- Maintains ordering of acknowledgments while respecting pause/resume semantics\\n- Allows pausing ACKs for specific resource types during config processing\\n- Supports head-of-line blocking mitigation\\n\\n**UpdateAck (update_ack.h)** - Data structure containing:\\n- The response nonce to acknowledge\\n- Error details for NACK responses\\n- Resource type URL\\n\\n## Failover Support\\n\\n**GrpcMuxFailover (grpc_mux_failover.h)** - Handles failover between primary and failover xDS sources:\\n- Arbitrates between primary and failover config providers\\n- Tracks connection state (ConnectingToPrimary, ConnectedToPrimary, etc.)\\n- Implements intelligent failover logic with retry mechanisms\\n\\n## Context and Configuration\\n\\n**GrpcMuxContext (grpc_mux_context.h)** - Data structure containing all context needed for creating a GrpcMux:\\n- Async client references\\n- Dispatcher and stats scope\\n- Rate limit settings\\n- Local info and config validators\\n- Backoff strategy\\n\\n## Legacy Implementation\\n\\nThe directory also contains legacy implementations:\\n- **GrpcMuxImpl (grpc_mux_impl.h/cc)** - Earlier SotW-only implementation\\n- **NewGrpcMuxImpl (new_grpc_mux_impl.h/cc)** - Delta-focused variant with older architecture\\n- **DeltaSubscriptionState (delta_subscription_state.h/cc)** - Older delta state implementation\\n\\n## Service Definition\\n\\n**api/envoy/service/discovery/v3/ads.proto** - Defines the gRPC service:\\n- StreamAggregatedResources: Bidirectional stream for SotW xDS\\n- DeltaAggregatedResources: Bidirectional stream for Delta xDS\\n- Both use DiscoveryRequest/DiscoveryResponse or DeltaDiscoveryRequest/DeltaDiscoveryResponse\\n\\nThe ADS implementation multiplexes multiple resource type subscriptions (LDS, CDS, EDS, RDS, etc.) onto a single gRPC stream for efficiency, coordinating subscription interest changes, handling ACK/NACK responses, and managing resource versioning for both incremental (delta) and full (state-of-the-world) update modes.\"\n}\n",

This includes:\\n\\n1. **GrpcMuxImpl (grpc_mux_impl.h/cc)** - A templated base class that manages subscriptions to one or more resource types. It implements two concrete variants:\\n   - GrpcMuxDelta: Implements Delta xDS protocol (incremental updates)\\n   - GrpcMuxSotw: Implements State-of-the-World xDS protocol (full resource snapshots)\\n   Both handle multiplexing multiple resource types (EDS, CDS, LDS, RDS) over a single gRPC stream.\\n\\n2. **Delta xDS State Machine (delta_subscription_state.h/cc)** - Tracks the protocol state of delta xDS sessions for individual resource types. Manages:\\n   - Requested resource tracking with per-resource versions\\n   - Wildcard vs specific resource subscriptions\\n   - Resource TTL (time-to-live) for heartbeat support\\n   - Subscription interest changes\\n\\n3. **SotW xDS State Machine (sotw_subscription_state.h/cc)** - Tracks state-of-the-world xDS sessions, managing version information and resource updates.\\n\\n4. **Subscription State Base Class (subscription_state.h)** - Provides the abstract BaseSubscriptionState template that both delta and SotW implementations inherit from. Handles:\\n   - ACK/NACK generation via getNextRequestWithAck()\\n   - Response handling through handleResponse()\\n   - Error detail formatting for rejections\\n\\n## gRPC Stream Handler\\n\\n**GrpcStream (grpc_stream.h)** - Manages the bidirectional gRPC stream to the xDS server. It:\\n- Establishes and maintains the connection\\n- Receives discovery responses via onReceiveMessage()\\n- Sends discovery requests\\n- Handles rate limiting and backoff strategy\\n- Implements Grpc::AsyncStreamCallbacks interface\\n\\n## Resource Subscription Tracking\\n\\n**WatchMap (watch_map.h/cc)** - Tracks subscriptions to xDS resources:\\n- Manages \\\"watches\\\" from different Envoy components (e.g., listeners, clusters) for the same resource\\n- Tracks which resource names are currently of interest\\n- Delivers updates to all interested watches\\n- Manages EDS resources cache for endpoint discovery\\n\\n## ACK/NACK Processing\\n\\n**PausableAckQueue (pausable_ack_queue.h/cc)** - Manages the queue of ACK/NACK messages:\\n- Maintains ordering of acknowledgments while respecting pause/resume semantics\\n- Allows pausing ACKs for specific resource types during config processing\\n- Supports head-of-line blocking mitigation\\n\\n**UpdateAck (update_ack.h)** - Data structure containing:\\n- The response nonce to acknowledge\\n- Error details for NACK responses\\n- Resource type URL\\n\\n## Failover Support\\n\\n**GrpcMuxFailover (grpc_mux_failover.h)** - Handles failover between primary and failover xDS sources:\\n- Arbitrates between primary and failover config providers\\n- Tracks connection state (ConnectingToPrimary, ConnectedToPrimary, etc.)\\n- Implements intelligent failover logic with retry mechanisms\\n\\n## Context and Configuration\\n\\n**GrpcMuxContext (grpc_mux_context.h)** - Data structure containing all context needed for creating a GrpcMux:\\n- Async client references\\n- Dispatcher and stats scope\\n- Rate limit settings\\n- Local info and config validators\\n- Backoff strategy\\n\\n## Legacy Implementation\\n\\nThe directory also contains legacy implementations:\\n- **GrpcMuxImpl (grpc_mux_impl.h/cc)** - Earlier SotW-only implementation\\n- **NewGrpcMuxImpl (new_grpc_mux_impl.h/cc)** - Delta-focused variant with older architecture\\n- **DeltaSubscriptionState (delta_subscription_state.h/cc)** - Older delta state implementation\\n\\n## Service Definition\\n\\n**api/envoy/service/discovery/v3/ads.proto** - Defines the gRPC service:\\n- StreamAggregatedResources: Bidirectional stream for SotW xDS\\n- DeltaAggregatedResources: Bidirectional stream for Delta xDS\\n- Both use DiscoveryRequest/DiscoveryResponse or DeltaDiscoveryRequest/DeltaDiscoveryResponse\\n\\nThe ADS implementation multiplexes multiple resource type subscriptions (LDS, CDS, EDS, RDS, etc.) onto a single gRPC stream for efficiency, coordinating subscription interest changes, handling ACK/NACK responses, and managing resource versioning for both incremental (delta) and full (state-of-the-world) update modes.\"\n}\n",
